Kira stood in the doorway of the living room, leaning on the frame, idly chewing the edge of a granola bar and watching the household without realizing she was smiling.

Jenna was on the floor, sketchbook in her lap, earbuds in. She swayed slightly to a rhythm only she could hear, tongue poking out in concentration as she added some final flourish to what looked like a doodle of Riley riding a velociraptor.

Riley was sprawled on the couch, one leg kicked over the back, flipping through a book with the kind of interest that was probably fake—until she started underlining things with a pen that absolutely wasn’t hers.

Carl had just finished limping in from the backyard, a little sweaty, hair damp at the edges. He tossed a pair of gloves on the table and muttered something about “tomato vines staging a coup.”

Kira, half-laughing:
You fight the plants. Win?

Carl, deadpan:
It was a draw. I have declared a truce until tomorrow.

Riley, not looking up:
He means the tomato cage fell and he almost died like a garden gnome.

Carl:
She’s not wrong.

Kira took a few steps into the room and sank into the chair across from Riley. She didn’t say anything for a while—just listened. Watched. Absorbed.

She felt like a puzzle piece that had finally stopped trying to fit into the wrong corner.

After a while, Riley looked up at her, eyebrow cocked.

Riley:
You’ve been quiet today.

Kira, shrugging:
Just thinking.

Jenna, pulling out one earbud:
Dangerous pastime.

Kira:
Yeah. But… good, I think?

She looked around at them—really looked. The chaos. The balance. The ease.

And something in her chest clicked.

Kira:
This whole thing… it’s weird.
But it’s also kind of amazing.
I don’t know what’s next, or what any of it means yet, but I’m not… afraid of it anymore.

Carl, from the doorway, soft but firm:
You don’t have to figure it all out now.
You just have to decide if you want to stay in it.

Kira smiled.

Kira:
I think I already have.

No big announcement. No confetti. Just the sound of three people silently knowing something had shifted again.

Fade to afternoon light slanting across the floor, the soft rustle of pages turning, and four people learning that sometimes home isn’t a place. It’s a choice you keep making—together.

So am I.

But no one moved.

Because fear, unlike love, didn’t ask for permission before settling into the space between them.

Fade to three women frozen in the kitchen, a fragile connection fraying, and the uneasy realization that love was never going to be the easy part.
